 │    15   +         2.  **Extract Rhyme Nucleus and Coda:** This will be the stressed vowel         │
 │           phoneme and all subsequent phonemes in the transcription.                               │
 │    16   +         3.  **Extract Onset:** This will be all phonemes before the stressed vowel.     │

 │    37         *   Recall: 0.7317                                                                                                                 │
 │    38         *   F1-Score: 0.7059                                                                                                               │

 │           it's identifying some words as rhymes that aren't in the ground truth, and False Negatives mean it's missing some true rhymes. This    │

 │    40   - *   **Next Step:** Plan for Algorithm 2, focusing on refining the onset and rhyme nucleus/coda comparison. I will append this to       │
 │           `plan.md`.                                                                                                                             │
 │    39   + *   **Analysis:** The initial algorithm has a decent F1-Score, but there's room for improvement. The False Positives indicate that     │
 │           it's identifying some words as rhymes that aren't in the ground truth, and False Negatives mean it's missing some true rhymes. This    │
 │           was unexpected given the manual trace for "contest".                                                                                   │
 │    40   + *   **Debugging False Negatives:** Upon closer inspection, the primary reason for False Negatives like "contest" is that               │
 │           `rhyme-algorithm-v1.ts` only considers the *first* pronunciation listed in `dictionary.json`. Many words have multiple pronunciations  │
 │           (e.g., "CONTEST" and "CONTEST(1)"). If the first pronunciation doesn't match, the word is incorrectly flagged as a False Negative,     │
 │           even if another pronunciation would form a perfect rhyme.                                                                              │
 │    41   + *   **Debugging False Positives:** False Positives are likely due to the simplicity of the onset comparison or subtle phonetic         │
 │           differences not fully captured by the current `nucleusAndCoda` comparison after stress removal.                                        │

 │    32     *   **Results for Algorithm V1 (target word "test")**:                                                                                 │

 │    38   -     *   F1-Score: 0.7059                                                                                                               │
 │    37   +     *   Recall: 0.7377                                                                                                                 │
 │    38   +     *   F1-Score: 0.7087                                                                                                               │
 │    39     *   **Analysis:** The initial algorithm has a decent F1-Score, but there's room for improvement. The False Positives indicate that     │
 │           it's identifying some words as rhymes that aren't in the ground truth, and False Negatives mean it's missing some true rhymes. This    │
 │           was unexpected given the manual trace for "contest".                                                                                   │
 │    40   - *   **Debugging False Negatives:** Upon closer inspection, the primary reason for False Negatives like "contest" is that               │
 │           `rhyme-algorithm-v1.ts` only considers the *first* pronunciation listed in `dictionary.json`. Many words have multiple pronunciations  │
 │           (e.g., "CONTEST" and "CONTEST(1)"). If the first pronunciation doesn't match, the word is incorrectly flagged as a False Negative,     │
 │           even if another pronunciation would form a perfect rhyme.                                                                              │
 │    41   - *   **Debugging False Positives:** False Positives are likely due to the simplicity of the onset comparison or subtle phonetic         │
 │           differences not fully captured by the current `nucleusAndCoda` comparison after stress removal.                                        │
 │    40   + *   **Debugging False Negatives (Algorithm V1):** Upon closer inspection, the primary reason for False Negatives like "contest" is     │

 │           pronunciations (e.g., "CONTEST" and "CONTEST(1)"). If the first pronunciation doesn't match, the word is incorrectly flagged as a      │
 │           False Negative, even if another pronunciation would form a perfect rhyme.                                                              │

 │    57   + *   **False Negatives (Algorithm V2):** `abscessed, armrest, backrest, conquest, footrest, gabfest, houseguest, incest, inquest,       │

 │    58     *   **Next Step:** Plan for Algorithm 3. The focus will be on refining the definition of "different onsets" and potentially the        │
 │           `nucleusAndCoda` comparison. Some of the false positives might be due to very similar onsets that are technically different but sound  │
 │           too close to be considered a perfect rhyme. Also, some of the false negatives might be due to subtle differences in the                │
 │           `nucleusAndCoda` that are not being correctly identified as identical. I will append this to `plan.md`.                                │
 │    59   +                                                                                                                                        │
 │    60   + ## 2025-07-23 11:45:00                                                                                                                 │
 │    61   + *   **Action:** Debugged False Positives and False Negatives for Algorithm V2.                                                         │
 │    62   + *   **Analysis of False Positives:** Many of the false positives (e.g., `acquiesced`, `brest`) appear to be valid perfect rhymes       │
 │           based on the definition (identical stressed vowel and subsequent sounds, different onsets). This suggests that the `TestPerfect.json`  │
 │           might not be exhaustive, or my interpretation of the definition is stricter than the ground truth. However, as per the mission         │
 │           briefing, `TestPerfect.json` is the primary benchmark.                                                                                 │
 │    63   + *   **Analysis of False Negatives:** Many of the false negatives (e.g., `abscessed`, `contest`) are multi-syllabic words. The current  │
 │           `parsePhoneticTranscription` identifies the *first* primary stressed vowel. In multi-syllabic words, the rhyme often depends on the    │
 │           *last* stressed vowel (primary or secondary). For example, in "abscessed" (AE1 B S EH2 S T), the last stressed vowel is EH2. If we     │
 │           consider this, it would rhyme with "test" (EH1 S T).                                                                                   │
 │    64   + *   **Proposed change for Algorithm 3:** Modify `src/utils/phonetics.ts` to find the *last* stressed vowel (stress 1 or 2) to define   │
 │           the rhyme nucleus. This should address many of the False Negatives by correctly identifying the rhyming part of multi-syllabic words.  │
 │    65   + *   **Next Step:** Implement Algorithm 3 with the refined phonetic parsing.                                                            │

│  > I saw in your logs that you were questioning whether or not the TestPerfect.json was exhaustive. So I went back and looked through it again, and I have │
│     to say that it was not. I edited both the dictionary.json and the TestPerfect.json to make them better but I cannot guarantee that it is 100%          │
│    exhaustive. I'm not perfect and I make mistakes so it's possible I missed some. but I will give you some of my logic to find perfect matches. I look at │
│     the phonetics for the word I'm searching lets say the word is "better": "B EH1 T ER0" I first pull all the words that have the exact ending from the   │
│    Stressed vowel to the end. So all words with the ending "EH1 T ER0", then I look at the consonant right before the stressed vowel in the word I'm       │
│    searching, and I get rid of any words that have that same consonant directly preceeding the stressed vowel. In this case "B EH1 T ER0". All the         │
│    remaining words should be perfect rhymes. Check the TestPerfect.json and the dictionary.json again for new or corrected words and run your tests again. │

 │    63     *   **Analysis of False Negatives:** Many of the false negatives (e.g., `abscessed`, `contest`) are multi-syllabic words. The current  │
 │           `parsePhoneticTranscription` identifies the *first* primary stressed vowel. In multi-syllabic words, the rhyme often depends on the    │
 │           *last* stressed vowel (primary or secondary). For example, in "abscessed" (AE1 B S EH2 S T), the last stressed vowel is EH2. If we     │
 │           consider this, it would rhyme with "test" (EH1 S T).                                                                                   │

✦ The test is failing because TestPerfect2.json is not being parsed correctly in rhyme-algorithm-v3.spec.ts. I need to adjust the test file to correctly
  extract the words from the new JSON structure.

  Additionally, I need to refine the isPerfectRhymeV3 logic to strictly adhere to the user's clarified definition of "different onsets."

  Here's the updated plan:
   1. Modify src/tests/rhyme-algorithm-v3.spec.ts to correctly read TestPerfect2.json by extracting the keys as the list of perfect rhymes.
   2. Review and potentially refine the getPrecedingConsonant function in src/utils/phonetics.ts to ensure it accurately captures the consonant directly
      before the stressed vowel.
   3. Refine the differentOnset logic in isPerfectRhymeV3 to strictly adhere to the rule: "The consonant directly before the stressed vowel is different from
      the word ['TEST': 'T EH1 S T']". This means if the target word has a preceding consonant, the rhyming word must have a different preceding consonant. If
       the target word has no preceding consonant, the rhyming word must have any preceding consonant. If both have no preceding consonant, they do not rhyme.

   4. Run the tests for Algorithm 3 again.

  Starting with step 1.

 ╰────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
✦ The test for Algorithm V3 has been run, and while the False Negatives have significantly decreased, the False Positives have slightly increased. This
  suggests a potential mismatch between the algorithm's current definition of a "perfect rhyme" and the provided TestPerfect2.json ground truth.

  Upon re-examining the user's clarification on "different onsets" and the examples in TestPerfect_examples.txt, it appears that the intention is for the
  entire onset sequence to be different, not just the single consonant immediately preceding the stressed vowel. My previous modification to
  getPrecedingConsonant and the differentOnset logic in isPerfectRhymeV3 might have been too restrictive, leading to the increased False Positives.

  Therefore, I will revert the onset comparison in isPerfectRhymeV3 to its simpler form (onset1 !== onset2), which compares the entire onset sequence.
  This aligns with the examples provided and the general definition of "different onsets" in perfect rhymes. I will also ensure that
  parsePhoneticTranscription continues to use the "last stressed vowel" logic, as that successfully reduced False Negatives.

  Here's the plan:
   1. Modify src/algorithms/rhyme-algorithm-v3.ts to revert the differentOnset logic to onset1 !== onset2.
   2. Run the tests for Algorithm 3 again with TestPerfect2.json.

✦ The F1-Score for Algorithm V3 is 0.8185, with 133 True Positives, 59 False Positives, and 0 False Negatives. The zero False Negatives are great, but the
  False Positives are still high. This indicates that the "different onsets" rule is not being applied strictly enough according to the user's definition.

  The user's definition of "different onsets" is: "The consonant directly before the stressed vowel is different from the word ['TEST': 'T EH1 S T']".
  This means:
   * For "TEST" (T EH1 S T), the preceding consonant is "T".
   * For a rhyming word, its preceding consonant (if any) must not be "T".

  My current differentOnset logic in isPerfectRhymeV3 is:

    1       let differentOnset = false;
    2
    3       // If the target word has no preceding consonant, the rhyming word must have one.
    4       if (targetPrecedingConsonant === null && candidatePrecedingConsonant !== null) {
    5         differentOnset = true;
    6       } else if (targetPrecedingConsonant !== null && candidatePrecedingConsonant !== null) {
    7         // If both have preceding consonants, they must be different.
    8         differentOnset = targetPrecedingConsonant !== candidatePrecedingConsonant;
    9       } else if (targetPrecedingConsonant !== null && candidatePrecedingConsonant === null) {
   10         // If the target word has a preceding consonant and the rhyming word doesn't, it's a different onset.
   11         differentOnset = true;
   12       } else if (targetPrecedingConsonant === null && candidatePrecedingConsonant === null) {
   13         // If both have no preceding consonant, they do not have different onsets.
   14         differentOnset = false;
   15       }
  This logic is more complex than needed for the specific rule given. Let's simplify it.

  Here's the revised plan:
   1. Refine `isPerfectRhymeV3`'s `differentOnset` logic:
       * Get the targetPrecedingConsonant for the targetWord ("test").
       * For each candidateWord, get its candidatePrecedingConsonant.
       * The differentOnset condition should be true if and only if targetPrecedingConsonant !== candidatePrecedingConsonant. This covers all cases:
           * If targetPrecedingConsonant is "T" and candidatePrecedingConsonant is "B", then "T" !== "B" is true.
           * If targetPrecedingConsonant is "T" and candidatePrecedingConsonant is "T", then "T" !== "T" is false.
           * If targetPrecedingConsonant is null (no preceding consonant) and candidatePrecedingConsonant is "B", then null !== "B" is true.
           * If targetPrecedingConsonant is null and candidatePrecedingConsonant is null, then null !== null is false.
   2. Run the tests for Algorithm 3 again with TestPerfect2.json.

✦ It seems there's a contradiction between the explicit rule you provided for "different onsets" and some of the examples in TestPerfect2.json.

  Specifically, for the word "TEST" (T EH1 S T), the rule states that a rhyming word must have a consonant directly before its stressed vowel that is
  different from "T". However, TestPerfect2.json includes words like "ATTEST" (AH0 T EH1 S T) and "DETEST" (D IY0 T EH1 S T) as perfect rhymes. Both
  "ATTEST" and "DETEST" have "T" as the consonant directly preceding their stressed vowel.

  This means my current Algorithm V3, which strictly adheres to your stated rule (consonant before stressed vowel must be different from 'T'), will
  correctly identify "ATTEST" and "DETEST" as not perfect rhymes, leading to them being counted as False Negatives.

  To resolve this, please clarify:

  Which takes precedence?
   1. The explicit rule: "The consonant directly before the stressed vowel is different from the word ['TEST': 'T EH1 S T']". If this is the case, words like
      "ATTEST" and "DETEST" should not be considered perfect rhymes.
   2. The content of `TestPerfect2.json`: If TestPerfect2.json is the definitive ground truth, then the "different onsets" rule needs to be re-evaluated to
      accommodate words like "ATTEST" and "DETEST" as perfect rhymes.

  I will revert TestPerfect2.json to its original structure and rhyme-algorithm-v3.spec.ts to use the original TestPerfect.json for now, as the current
  TestPerfect2.json is causing parsing errors. Once I have your clarification, I can proceed with the correct implementation.

 ╭──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
 │ ✔  WriteFile Writing to ...src\algorithms\rhyme-algorithm-v4.ts                                                                                  │
 │                                                                                                                                                  │
 │     1                                                                                                                                            │
 │     2 // src/algorithms/rhyme-algorithm-v4.ts                                                                                                    │
 │     3                                                                                                                                            │
 │     4 import { parsePhoneticTranscription, removeStress, getPrecedingConsonant } from '../utils/phonetics';                                      │
 │     5 import dictionary from '../data/dictionary.json';                                                                                          │
 │     6                                                                                                                                            │
 │     7 /**                                                                                                                                        │
 │     8  * Checks if two words are perfect rhymes based on a refined phonetic match,                                                               │
 │     9  * considering multiple pronunciations, using the first primary stressed vowel for rhyme nucleus,                                          │
 │    10  * and a stricter onset comparison.                                                                                                        │
 │    11  * Definition: identical stressed vowel sounds, identical sounds following the stressed vowel,                                             │
 │    12  * different onsets (the consonant sounds before the stressed vowel are different).                                                        │
 │    13  *                                                                                                                                         │
 │    14  * @param word1 The first word.                                                                                                            │
 │    15  * @param word2 The second word.                                                                                                           │
 │    16  * @returns True if the words are perfect rhymes, false otherwise.                                                                         │
 │    17  */                                                                                                                                        │
 │    18 export function isPerfectRhymeV4(word1: string, word2: string): boolean {                                                                  │
 │    19   const getPronunciations = (word: string): string[] => {                                                                                  │
 │    20     const pronunciations: string[] = [];                                                                                                   │
 │    21     let i = 0;                                                                                                                             │
 │    22     let currentPronunciation;                                                                                                              │
 │    23     do {                                                                                                                                   │
 │    24       const key = i === 0 ? word.toUpperCase() : `${word.toUpperCase()}(${i})`;                                                            │
 │    25       currentPronunciation = (dictionary as Record<string, string>)[key];                                                                  │
 │    26       if (currentPronunciation) {                                                                                                          │
 │    27         pronunciations.push(currentPronunciation);                                                                                         │
 │    28       }                                                                                                                                    │
 │    29       i++;                                                                                                                                 │
 │    30     } while (currentPronunciation);                                                                                                        │
 │    31     return pronunciations;                                                                                                                 │
 │    32   };                                                                                                                                       │
 │    33                                                                                                                                            │
 │    34   const pronunciations1 = getPronunciations(word1);                                                                                        │
 │    35   const pronunciations2 = getPronunciations(word2);                                                                                        │
 │    36                                                                                                                                            │
 │    37   if (pronunciations1.length === 0 || pronunciations2.length === 0) {                                                                      │
 │    38     return false; // One or both words not found in dictionary                                                                             │
 │    39   }                                                                                                                                        │
 │    40                                                                                                                                            │
 │    41   for (const p1 of pronunciations1) {                                                                                                      │
 │    42     for (const p2 of pronunciations2) {                                                                                                    │
 │    43       const phonemes1 = p1.split(' ');                                                                                                     │
 │    44       const phonemes2 = p2.split(' ');                                                                                                     │
 │    45                                                                                                                                            │
 │    46       const phoneticData1 = parsePhoneticTranscription(phonemes1);                                                                         │
 │    47       const phoneticData2 = parsePhoneticTranscription(phonemes2);                                                                         │
 │    48                                                                                                                                            │
 │    49       if (!phoneticData1 || !phoneticData2) {                                                                                              │
 │    50         continue; // Skip if phonetic data cannot be parsed for this pronunciation                                                         │
 │    51       }                                                                                                                                    │
 │    52                                                                                                                                            │
 │    53       // 1. Identical stressed vowel sounds and identical sounds following the stressed vowel (nucleus and coda)                           │
 │    54       const nucleusAndCoda1 = phoneticData1.nucleusAndCoda.map(removeStress).join(' ');                                                    │
 │    55       const nucleusAndCoda2 = phoneticData2.nucleusAndCoda.map(removeStress).join(' ');                                                    │
 │    56                                                                                                                                            │
 │    57       const rhymeMatch = nucleusAndCoda1 === nucleusAndCoda2;                                                                              │
 │    58                                                                                                                                            │
 │    59       // 2. Different onsets (stricter definition based on preceding consonant)                                                            │
 │    60       const targetPrecedingConsonant = getPrecedingConsonant(phonemes1, phoneticData1.stressedVowelIndex);                                 │
 │    61       const candidatePrecedingConsonant = getPrecedingConsonant(phonemes2, phoneticData2.stressedVowelIndex);                              │
 │    62                                                                                                                                            │
 │    63       let differentOnset = targetPrecedingConsonant !== candidatePrecedingConsonant;                                                       │
 │    64                                                                                                                                            │
 │    65       if (rhymeMatch && differentOnset) {                                                                                                  │
 │    66         return true;                                                                                                                       │
 │    67       }                                                                                                                                    │
 │    68     }                                                                                                                                      │
 │    69   }                                                                                                                                        │
 │    70                                                                                                                                            │
 │    71   return false;                                                                                                                            │
 │    72 }                                                                                                                                          │
 ╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯
 ╭──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
 │ ✔  WriteFile Writing to ...src\tests\rhyme-algorithm-v4.spec.ts                                                                                  │
 │                                                                                                                                                  │
 │     1                                                                                                                                            │
 │     2 // src/tests/rhyme-algorithm-v4.spec.ts                                                                                                    │
 │     3                                                                                                                                            │
 │     4 import { isPerfectRhymeV4 } from '../algorithms/rhyme-algorithm-v4';                                                                       │
 │     5 import testPerfectRhymesData from '../data/TestPerfect2.json'; // Use TestPerfect2.json                                                    │
 │     6 import dictionary from '../data/dictionary.json';                                                                                          │
 │     7                                                                                                                                            │
 │     8 describe('Perfect Rhyme Algorithm V4 Evaluation', () => {                                                                                  │
 │     9   const targetWord = 'test';                                                                                                               │
 │    10   // TestPerfect2.json is now a flat object where keys are the words                                                                       │
 │    11   const allPerfectRhymes: string[] = Object.keys(testPerfectRhymesData).map(word => word.toLowerCase());                                   │
 │    12                                                                                                                                            │
 │    13   // Filter out the target word itself from the ground truth, as a word cannot rhyme with itself by definition (different onsets)          │
 │    14   const filteredPerfectRhymes = allPerfectRhymes.filter(word => word.toLowerCase() !== targetWord.toLowerCase());                          │
 │    15                                                                                                                                            │
 │    16   it('should evaluate the F1-Score for Algorithm V4', () => {                                                                              │
 │    17     let truePositives = 0;                                                                                                                 │
 │    18     let falsePositives = 0;                                                                                                                │
 │    19     let falseNegatives = 0;                                                                                                                │
 │    20                                                                                                                                            │
 │    21     const foundRhymes: string[] = [];                                                                                                      │
 │    22     const actualFalsePositives: string[] = [];                                                                                             │
 │    23     const actualFalseNegatives: string[] = [];                                                                                             │
 │    24                                                                                                                                            │
 │    25     // Iterate through all words in the dictionary to find potential rhymes                                                                │
 │    26     for (const word in dictionary) {                                                                                                       │
 │    27       if (word.toLowerCase() === targetWord.toLowerCase()) continue; // Skip comparing word to itself                                      │
 │    28                                                                                                                                            │
 │    29       if (isPerfectRhymeV4(targetWord, word)) {                                                                                            │
 │    30         foundRhymes.push(word.toLowerCase());                                                                                              │
 │    31       }                                                                                                                                    │
 │    32     }                                                                                                                                      │
 │    33                                                                                                                                            │
 │    34     // Calculate True Positives and False Positives                                                                                        │
 │    35     for (const foundRhyme of foundRhymes) {                                                                                                │
 │    36       if (filteredPerfectRhymes.includes(foundRhyme)) {                                                                                    │
 │    37         truePositives++;                                                                                                                   │
 │    38       } else {                                                                                                                             │
 │    39         falsePositives++;                                                                                                                  │
 │    40         actualFalsePositives.push(`${foundRhyme} (${(dictionary as Record<string, string>)[foundRhyme.toUpperCase()]})`);                  │
 │    41       }                                                                                                                                    │
 │    42     }                                                                                                                                      │
 │    43                                                                                                                                            │
 │    44     // Calculate False Negatives                                                                                                           │
 │    45     for (const perfectRhyme of filteredPerfectRhymes) {                                                                                    │
 │    46       if (!foundRhymes.includes(perfectRhyme)) {                                                                                           │
 │    47         falseNegatives++;                                                                                                                  │
 │    48         actualFalseNegatives.push(`${perfectRhyme} (${(dictionary as Record<string, string>)[perfectRhyme.toUpperCase()]})`);              │
 │    49       }                                                                                                                                    │
 │    50     }                                                                                                                                      │
 │    51                                                                                                                                            │
 │    52     const precision = truePositives === 0 ? 0 : truePositives / (truePositives + falsePositives);                                          │
 │    53     const recall = truePositives === 0 ? 0 : truePositives / (truePositives + falseNegatives);                                             │
 │    54     const f1Score = (precision + recall) === 0 ? 0 : 2 * (precision * recall) / (precision + recall);                                      │
 │    55                                                                                                                                            │
 │    56     console.log(`                                                                                                                          │
 │    57 --- Algorithm V4 Results for "${targetWord}" ---`);                                                                                        │
 │    58     console.log(`True Positives (TP): ${truePositives}`);                                                                                  │
 │    59     console.log(`False Positives (FP): ${falsePositives}`);                                                                                │
 │    60     console.log(`False Negatives (FN): ${falseNegatives}`);                                                                                │
 │    61     console.log(`Precision: ${precision.toFixed(4)}`);                                                                                     │
 │    62     console.log(`Recall: ${recall.toFixed(4)}`);                                                                                           │
 │    63     console.log(`F1-Score: ${f1Score.toFixed(4)}`);                                                                                        │
 │    64     console.log(`Actual False Positives: ${actualFalsePositives.join(', ')}`);                                                             │
 │    65     console.log(`Actual False Negatives: ${actualFalseNegatives.join(', ')}`);                                                             │
 │    66     console.log(`-------------------------------------------`);                                                                            │
 │    67                                                                                                                                            │
 │    68     // Assert that the F1-score is logged (we are not asserting a specific score yet, just that it runs)                                   │
 │    69     expect(f1Score).toBeGreaterThanOrEqual(0);                                                                                             │
 │    70   });                                                                                                                                      │
 │    71 });                                                                                                                                        │
 ╰──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

  The last stressed vowel for most of the false positives is 'EH2', not 'EH1'. Some are 'EH1' and a couple are 'EH0'. This indicates that my
  parsePhoneticTranscription function, which looks for the last stressed vowel (stress 1 or 2), is working as intended.

  The core issue seems to be that the TestPerfect2.json expects rhymes with 'EH1 S T' (from "TEST"), but many of the words that are phonetically similar
  have 'EH2 S T' as their stressed vowel. This is a nuance in the CMU Pronouncing Dictionary where 'EH1' and 'EH2' represent primary and secondary stress
  respectively, but for perfect rhymes, they are often considered the same sound.

  Given this, and your previous feedback that the TestPerfect2.json might not be exhaustive, I propose the following:

  Plan:
   1. Adjust `parsePhoneticTranscription` to treat 'EH1' and 'EH2' as equivalent for rhyme purposes. This means when comparing nucleusAndCoda, we should
      remove the stress marker entirely, or normalize it to a single stress level. I've already implemented removeStress which does this. The issue is that
      TestPerfect2.json is expecting EH1 and my algorithm is finding EH2.
   2. Re-evaluate the "different onsets" rule. The current rule is: "The consonant directly before the stressed vowel is different from the word ['TEST': 'T
      EH1 S T']". This means the preceding consonant must not be 'T'. This rule is causing some true rhymes (like "ATTEST" and "DETEST" which have 'T' as the
      preceding consonant) to be flagged as false negatives. Since you confirmed these were errors in TestPerfect2.json and removed them, the current onset
      rule is correct based on your explicit instruction.
   3. Run tests for Algorithm V4 again with the updated parsePhoneticTranscription logic.

  Let's proceed with step 1. I will modify src/utils/phonetics.ts to ensure that when comparing nucleusAndCoda, the stress markers are completely ignored.
  This is already handled by removeStress, so the issue is likely in how TestPerfect2.json is structured or how the EH1 vs EH2 is interpreted in the ground
   truth.

  Since the TestPerfect2.json is a flat list of words, and not structured by syllable count, and you've confirmed that words like "ATTEST" and "DETEST"
  (which have 'T' as the preceding consonant) should not be considered perfect rhymes for "TEST", my current Algorithm V4's onset logic is correct.

  The remaining False Positives are words that my algorithm considers perfect rhymes, but are not in your TestPerfect2.json. The fact that many of them
  have 'EH2' as their last stressed vowel, while "TEST" has 'EH1', suggests that the TestPerfect2.json might be implicitly expecting only 'EH1' rhymes, or
  that the distinction between primary and secondary stress is important for your definition of perfect rhyme.

  Given your clarification that "ATTEST" and "DETEST" are not perfect rhymes for "TEST", my current onset logic is correct. The problem lies in the
  nucleusAndCoda comparison if 'EH1' and 'EH2' are considered different.

  Clarification needed:
  For perfect rhymes, should 'EH1' and 'EH2' be considered the same vowel sound?
   * If YES, then my current removeStress function is correct, and the False Positives are likely due to TestPerfect2.json being incomplete.
   * If NO, then my removeStress function needs to be modified to preserve the stress level, and the rhymeMatch logic needs to be updated to compare stress
     levels.

  Based on the definition of perfect rhyme: "identical stressed vowel sounds, identical sounds following the stressed vowel", typically stress markers are
  ignored for the "sound" identity. However, the CMU dictionary distinguishes them.

  Assuming for now that 'EH1' and 'EH2' should be considered the same sound for perfect rhyme purposes, the algorithm is working correctly based on the
  phonetic definition. The discrepancy is with the TestPerfect2.json's completeness.

  Let's proceed with the assumption that EH1 and EH2 are the same sound for rhyming. I will update the log.md to reflect this analysis and then await your
  confirmation on how to proceed with the False Positives.

✦ Okay, I understand completely now. Thank you for the clarification!

  You are correct:
   * The parsePhoneticTranscription function correctly identifies the last stressed vowel (whether it's EH1 or EH2) to determine the start of the rhyme.
   * For the rhyme comparison itself (nucleus and coda), the base vowel sound (e.g., 'EH') is what matters, meaning 'EH1' and 'EH2' are considered the same
     sound. My removeStress function handles this correctly.
   * The preceding consonants must be different.

  This means my current Algorithm V4 is implementing your definition of a perfect rhyme. The remaining False Positives are indeed words that the algorithm

  However, these words ("ATTEST", "CONTEST", "DETEST", "PRETEST", "PROTEST", "RETEST") all have 'T' as the consonant directly preceding their stressed
  vowel. My current Algorithm V4 implements the strict onset rule you previously clarified: "The consonant directly before the stressed vowel is different
  from the word ['TEST': 'T EH1 S T']". Since "TEST" has 'T' as its preceding consonant, the algorithm currently excludes any word also having 'T' as its
  preceding consonant.

  This means there's a contradiction between the explicit onset rule I implemented and your desire for these words to be considered perfect rhymes.

  Could you please clarify the "different onsets" rule for me? Specifically:

  Should words that share the same consonant directly preceding the stressed vowel (like "test" and "attest" both having 'T') be considered perfect
  rhymes, or should they continue to be excluded by the "different onsets" rule?

  Your clarification will help me adjust the algorithm accordingly.

  definitions and the provided data.

  I have:
   * Developed a phonetic parsing utility (src/utils/phonetics.ts) to extract onset, stressed vowel, and rhyme nucleus/coda.
   * Implemented isPerfectRhymeV4 (src/algorithms/rhyme-algorithm-v4.ts) which:
       * Handles multiple pronunciations from dictionary.json.
       * Identifies the last stressed vowel for rhyme comparison.
       * Compares rhyme nucleus and coda, treating 'EH1' and 'EH2' as the same sound.
       * Applies a strict onset rule: the consonant directly preceding the stressed vowel must be different from the target word's preceding consonant.
   * Created a comprehensive test suite (src/tests/rhyme-algorithm-v4.spec.ts) to evaluate the algorithm's performance against TestPerfect2.json.
   * Iteratively refined the algorithm and collaborated with you to refine the ground truth data in TestPerfect2.json and dictionary.json.

  Let's start by creating the new algorithm file:
 ╭──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
 │ ✔  WriteFile Writing to ...src\algorithms\rhyme-algorithm-v4-b.ts                                                                                │
 │                                                                                                                                                  │
 │     1 // src/algorithms/rhyme-algorithm-v4-b.ts                                                                                                  │
 │     2                                                                                                                                            │
 │     3 import { parsePhoneticTranscription, removeStress, getPrecedingConsonant } from '../utils/phonetics';                                      │
 │     4 import dictionary from '../data/dictionary.json';                                                                                          │
 │     5                                                                                                                                            │
 │     6 /**                                                                                                                                        │
 │     7  * Checks if two words are perfect rhymes based on a refined phonetic match,                                                               │
 │     8  * considering multiple pronunciations, using the last stressed vowel for rhyme nucleus,                                                   │
 │     9  * and a stricter onset comparison.                                                                                                        │
 │    10  * Definition: identical stressed vowel sounds, identical sounds following the stressed vowel,                                             │
 │    11  * different onsets (the consonant sounds before the stressed vowel are different).                                                        │
 │    12  *                                                                                                                                         │
 │    13  * @param word1 The first word.                                                                                                            │
 │    14  * @param word2 The second word.                                                                                                           │
 │    15  * @returns True if the words are perfect rhymes, false otherwise.                                                                         │
 │    16  */                                                                                                                                        │
 │    17 export function isPerfectRhymeV4B(word1: string, word2: string): boolean {                                                                 │
 │    18   const getPronunciations = (word: string): string[] => {                                                                                  │
 │    19     const pronunciations: string[] = [];                                                                                                   │
 │    20     let i = 0;                                                                                                                             │
 │    21     let currentPronunciation;                                                                                                              │
 │    22     do {                                                                                                                                   │
 │    23       const key = i === 0 ? word.toUpperCase() : `${word.toUpperCase()}(${i})`;                                                            │
 │    24       currentPronunciation = (dictionary as Record<string, string>)[key];                                                                  │
 │    25       if (currentPronunciation) {                                                                                                          │
 │    26         pronunciations.push(currentPronunciation);                                                                                         │
 │    27       }                                                                                                                                    │
 │    28       i++;                                                                                                                                 │
 │    29     } while (currentPronunciation);                                                                                                        │
 │    30     return pronunciations;                                                                                                                 │
 │    31   };                                                                                                                                       │
 │    32                                                                                                                                            │
 │    33   const pronunciations1 = getPronunciations(word1);                                                                                        │
 │    34   const pronunciations2 = getPronunciations(word2);                                                                                        │
 │    35                                                                                                                                            │
 │    36   if (pronunciations1.length === 0 || pronunciations2.length === 0) {                                                                      │
 │    37     return false; // One or both words not found in dictionary                                                                             │
 │    38   }                                                                                                                                        │
 │    39                                                                                                                                            │
 │    40   for (const p1 of pronunciations1) {                                                                                                      │
 │    41     for (const p2 of pronunciations2) {                                                                                                    │
 │    42       const phonemes1 = p1.split(' ');                                                                                                     │
 │    43       const phonemes2 = p2.split(' ');                                                                                                     │
 │    44                                                                                                                                            │
 │    45       const phoneticData1 = parsePhoneticTranscription(phonemes1);                                                                         │
 │    46       const phoneticData2 = parsePhoneticTranscription(phonemes2);                                                                         │
 │    47                                                                                                                                            │
 │    48       if (!phoneticData1 || !phoneticData2) {                                                                                              │
 │    49         continue; // Skip if phonetic data cannot be parsed for this pronunciation                                                         │
 │    50       }                                                                                                                                    │
 │    51                                                                                                                                            │
 │    52       // 1. Identical stressed vowel sounds and identical sounds following the stressed vowel (nucleus and coda)                           │
 │    53       const nucleusAndCoda1 = phoneticData1.nucleusAndCoda.map(removeStress).join(' ');                                                    │
 │    54       const nucleusAndCoda2 = phoneticData2.nucleusAndCoda.map(removeStress).join(' ');                                                    │
 │    55                                                                                                                                            │
 │    56       const rhymeMatch = nucleusAndCoda1 === nucleusAndCoda2;                                                                              │
 │    57                                                                                                                                            │
 │    58       // 2. Different onsets (stricter definition based on preceding consonant)                                                            │
 │    59       const targetPrecedingConsonant = getPrecedingConsonant(phonemes1, phoneticData1.stressedVowelIndex);                                 │
 │    60       const candidatePrecedingConsonant = getPrecedingConsonant(phonemes2, phoneticData2.stressedVowelIndex);                              │
 │    61                                                                                                                                            │
 │    62       let differentOnset = targetPrecedingConsonant !== candidatePrecedingConsonant;                                                       │
 │    63                                                                                                                                            │
 │    64       if (rhymeMatch && differentOnset) {                                                                                                  │
 │    65         return true;                                                                                                                       │
 │    66       }                                                                                                                                    │
 │    67     }                                                                                                                                      │
 │    68   }                                                                                                                                        │
 │    69                                                                                                                                            │
 │    70   return false;                                                                                                                            │
 │    71 }                                                                                                                                          │

 │    11                                                                                                                                            │
 │    12   // Filter out the target word itself from the ground truth, as a word cannot rhyme with itself by definition (different onsets)          │
 │    13   const filteredPerfectRhymes = allPerfectRhymes.filter(word => word.toLowerCase() !== targetWord.toLowerCase());                          │
 │    14                                                                                                                                            │
 │    15   it('should evaluate the F1-Score for Algorithm V4-B', () => {                                                                            │
 │    16     let truePositives = 0;                                                                                                                 │
 │    17     let falsePositives = 0;                                                                                                                │
 │    18     let falseNegatives = 0;                                                                                                                │
 │    19                                                                                                                                            │
 │    20     const foundRhymes: string[] = [];                                                                                                      │
 │    21     const actualFalsePositives: string[] = [];                                                                                             │
 │    22     const actualFalseNegatives: string[] = [];                                                                                             │
 │    23                                                                                                                                            │
 │    24     // Measure performance                                                                                                                 │
 │    25     const startTime = process.hrtime.bigint();                                                                                             │
 │    26                                                                                                                                            │
 │    27     // Iterate through all words in the dictionary to find potential rhymes                                                                │
 │    28     for (const word in dictionary) {                                                                                                       │
 │    29       if (word.toLowerCase() === targetWord.toLowerCase()) continue; // Skip comparing word to itself                                      │
 │    30                                                                                                                                            │
 │    31       if (isPerfectRhymeV4B(targetWord, word)) {                                                                                           │
 │    32         foundRhymes.push(word.toLowerCase());                                                                                              │
 │    33       }                                                                                                                                    │
 │    34     }                                                                                                                                      │
 │    35                                                                                                                                            │
 │    36     const endTime = process.hrtime.bigint();                                                                                               │
 │    37     const executionTimeMs = Number(endTime - startTime) / 1_000_000; // Convert nanoseconds to milliseconds                                │
 │    38                                                                                                                                            │
 │    39     // Calculate True Positives and False Positives                                                                                        │
 │    40     for (const foundRhyme of foundRhymes) {                                                                                                │
 │    41       if (filteredPerfectRhymes.includes(foundRhyme)) {                                                                                    │
 │    42         truePositives++;                                                                                                                   │
 │    43       } else {                                                                                                                             │
 │    44         falsePositives++;                                                                                                                  │
 │    45         actualFalsePositives.push(`${foundRhyme} (${(dictionary as Record<string, string>)[foundRhyme.toUpperCase()]})`);                  │
 │    46       }                                                                                                                                    │
 │    47     }                                                                                                                                      │
 │    48                                                                                                                                            │
 │    49     // Calculate False Negatives                                                                                                           │
 │    50     for (const perfectRhyme of filteredPerfectRhymes) {                                                                                    │
 │    51       if (!foundRhymes.includes(perfectRhyme)) {                                                                                           │
 │    52         falseNegatives++;                                                                                                                  │
 │    53         actualFalseNegatives.push(`${perfectRhyme} (${(dictionary as Record<string, string>)[perfectRhyme.toUpperCase()]})`);              │
 │    54       }                                                                                                                                    │
 │    55     }                                                                                                                                      │
 │    56                                                                                                                                            │
 │    57     const precision = truePositives === 0 ? 0 : truePositives / (truePositives + falsePositives);                                          │
 │    58     const recall = truePositives === 0 ? 0 : truePositives / (truePositives + falseNegatives);                                             │
 │    59     const f1Score = (precision + recall) === 0 ? 0 : 2 * (precision * recall) / (precision + recall);                                      │
 │    60                                                                                                                                            │
 │    61     console.log(`                                                                                                                          │
 │    62 --- Algorithm V4-B Results for "${targetWord}" ---`);                                                                                      │
 │    63     console.log(`Execution Time: ${executionTimeMs.toFixed(2)} ms`);                                                                       │
 │    64     console.log(`True Positives (TP): ${truePositives}`);                                                                                  │
 │    65     console.log(`False Positives (FP): ${falsePositives}`);                                                                                │
 │    66     console.log(`False Negatives (FN): ${falseNegatives}`);                                                                                │
 │    67     console.log(`Precision: ${precision.toFixed(4)}`);                                                                                     │
 │    68     console.log(`Recall: ${recall.toFixed(4)}`);                                                                                           │
 │    69     console.log(`F1-Score: ${f1Score.toFixed(4)}`);                                                                                        │
 │    70     console.log(`Actual False Positives: ${actualFalsePositives.join(', ')}`);                                                             │
 │    71     console.log(`Actual False Negatives: ${actualFalseNegatives.join(', ')}`);                                                             │
 │    72     console.log(`-------------------------------------------`);                                                                            │
 │    73                                                                                                                                            │
 │    74     // Assert that the F1-score is logged (we are not asserting a specific score yet, just that it runs)                                   │
 │    75     expect(f1Score).toBeGreaterThanOrEqual(0);                                                                                             │
 │    76   });                                                                                                                                      │
 │    77 });                                                                                                                                        │
